class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">John Barry (composer)</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vcard plainlist" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background-color: #bfe0bf"><span class="fn">John Barry</span><br /><span class="honorific-suffix" style="font-size: 77%; font-weight: normal;"><a href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">OBE</a></span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a href="/wiki/File:John-barry-2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="John-barry-2006.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/John-barry-2006.jpg/180px-John-barry-2006.jpg" width="180" height="200" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f8/John-barry-2006.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="222" /></a><div>John Barry at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, London, September 2006</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #bfe0bf">Background information</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap">Birth name</span></th><td class="nickname">\nJohn Barry Prendergast</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Born</th><td>\n<span style="display:none">(<span class="bday">1933-11-03</span>)</span>3 November 1933<br /><a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>, England</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Died</th><td>\n30 January 2011<span style="display:none">(2011-01-30)</span> (aged&#160;77)<br /><a href="/wiki/Oyster_Bay_(town),_New_York" title="Oyster Bay (town), New York">Oyster Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_(state)" title="New York (state)">New York</a>, U.S.</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Genres</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">Film score</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap">Occupation(s)</span></th><td class="role">\nComposer, conductor</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Instruments</th><td class="note">\n<div class="hlist hlist-separated"><ul><li>Keyboards</li><li>drums</li><li>harmonica</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><span class="nowrap">Years active</span></th><td>\n1959\xe2\x80\x932006</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>John Barry Prendergast</b>, <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">OBE</a></span> (3 November 1933&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 30 January 2011)<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-one-india_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-one-india-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> was an English composer and conductor of film music. He composed the scores for 11 of the <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond</a></i> films between 1963 and 1987, and also arranged and performed the "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme" title="James Bond Theme">James Bond Theme</a>" to the first film in the series, 1962\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(film)" title="Dr. No (film)">Dr. No</a></i>. He wrote the Grammy- and Academy Award-winning scores to the films <i><a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Wolves" title="Dances with Wolves">Dances with Wolves</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Out_of_Africa_(film)" title="Out of Africa (film)">Out of Africa</a></i>, as well as the theme for the British television cult series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Persuaders!" title="The Persuaders!">The Persuaders!</a></i>, in a career spanning over 50 years. In 1999, he was appointed OBE at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> for services to music.\n</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, Barry spent his early years working in cinemas owned by his father. During his <a href="/wiki/National_service" title="National service">national service</a> with the British Army in Cyprus, Barry began performing as a musician after learning to play the trumpet. Upon completing his national service, he formed his own band in 1957, <a href="/wiki/The_John_Barry_Seven" title="The John Barry Seven">The John Barry Seven</a>. He later developed an interest in composing and arranging music, making his d\xc3\xa9but for television in 1958. He came to the notice of the makers of the first James Bond film <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(film)" title="Dr. No (film)">Dr. No</a></i>, who were dissatisfied with a theme for <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> given to them by <a href="/wiki/Monty_Norman" title="Monty Norman">Monty Norman</a>. This started a successful association between Barry and <a href="/wiki/Eon_Productions" title="Eon Productions">Eon Productions</a> that lasted for 25 years.\n</p><p>He received many awards for his work, including five <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>; two for <i><a href="/wiki/Born_Free" title="Born Free">Born Free</a></i>, and one each for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_in_Winter_(1968_film)" title="The Lion in Winter (1968 film)">The Lion in Winter</a></i> (for which he also won the first <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Film_Music" title="BAFTA Award for Best Film Music">BAFTA Award for Best Film Music</a>), <i>Dances with Wolves</i> and <i>Out of Africa</i> (both of which also won him <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>). He also received ten <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award" title="Golden Globe Award">Golden Globe Award</a> nominations, winning once for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Score</a> for <i>Out of Africa</i> in 1986. Barry completed his last film score, <a href="/wiki/Enigma_(2001_film)" title="Enigma (2001 film)"><i>Enigma</i></a>, in 2001 and recorded the successful album <i><a href="/wiki/Eternal_Echoes" title="Eternal Echoes">Eternal Echoes</a></i> the same year. He then concentrated chiefly on live performances and co-wrote the music to the musical <i>Brighton Rock</i> in 2004 alongside <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a>. In 2001, Barry became a Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" class="mw-redirect" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a>, and, in 2005, he was made a Fellow of the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">British Academy of Film and Television Arts</a>. Barry was married four times and had four children. He moved to the United States in 1975 and lived there for the remainder of his life until his death in 2011.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Other_film_scores"><span class="tocnumber">3.2</span> <span class="toctext">Other film scores</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biography">Biography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Biography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early life and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Barry was born John Barry Prendergast, in <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a>, England, and was the son of an English mother and an Irish father. His mother was a classical pianist. His father, John Xavier "Jack" Prendergast, from <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a>, was a <a href="/wiki/Projectionist" title="Projectionist">projectionist</a> during the silent film era, who later owned a chain of cinemas across <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">northern England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Irish_Times_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irish_Times-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Obit_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Obit-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Yorshire_Post_Obit_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yorshire_Post_Obit-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> As a result of his father\'s work, Barry was raised in and around cinemas in northern England<sup id="cite_ref-Irish_Times_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Irish_Times-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> and he later stated that this childhood background influenced his musical tastes and interests.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Obit_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Obit-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Barry was educated at <a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_School,_York" title="St Peter&#39;s School, York">St Peter\'s School, York</a>, and also received composition lessons from <a href="/wiki/Francis_Jackson_(composer)" title="Francis Jackson (composer)">Francis Jackson</a>, Organist of <a href="/wiki/York_Minster" title="York Minster">York Minster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Obit_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Obit-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Serving in the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>, Barry spent his national service playing the trumpet.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> During his army service, he took a correspondence course (with <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a> composer <a href="/wiki/William_Russo_(musician)" title="William Russo (musician)">Bill Russo</a>); he also worked as an <a href="/wiki/Arrangement" title="Arrangement">arranger</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Jack_Parnell" title="Jack Parnell">Jack Parnell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Heath_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ted Heath (musician)">Ted Heath\'s Orchestra</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_Obit_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_Obit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and formed his own band in 1957, <a href="/wiki/The_John_Barry_Seven" title="The John Barry Seven">the John Barry Seven</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> with whom he had some hit records on <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Graphophone_Company" title="Columbia Graphophone Company">EMI\'s Columbia</a> label. These included "Hit and Miss", the theme tune he composed for the BBC\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Juke_Box_Jury" title="Juke Box Jury">Juke Box Jury</a></i> programme, a cover of the <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Smith" title="Johnny Smith">Johnny Smith</a> song "<a href="/wiki/Walk_Don%27t_Run_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Walk Don&#39;t Run (song)">Walk Don\'t Run</a>", and a cover of the theme for the <a href="/wiki/United_Artists" title="United Artists">United Artists</a> western <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magnificent_Seven" title="The Magnificent Seven">The Magnificent Seven</a></i>.\n</p><p>By 1959 Barry was gaining commissions to arrange music for other acts, starting with a young trio on Decca, coincidentally called the Three Barry Sisters, though unrelated both to Barry and the more famous Barry Sisters duo in America.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The career breakthrough for Barry was the BBC television series <i><a href="/wiki/Drumbeat_(TV_series)" title="Drumbeat (TV series)">Drumbeat</a></i>, when he appeared with the John Barry Seven. He was employed by <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> from 1959 until 1962 arranging orchestral accompaniment for the company\'s singers, including <a href="/wiki/Adam_Faith" title="Adam Faith">Adam Faith</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> he also composed songs (along with <a href="/wiki/Les_Vandyke" title="Les Vandyke">Les Vandyke</a>) and scores for films in which Faith was featured. When Faith made his first film, <i><a href="/wiki/Beat_Girl" title="Beat Girl">Beat Girl</a></i> (1960), Barry composed, arranged and conducted the score, his first. His music was later released as the UK\'s first soundtrack album.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barry also composed the music for another Faith film, <i><a href="/wiki/Never_Let_Go" title="Never Let Go">Never Let Go</a></i> (also 1960), orchestrated the score for <i><a href="/wiki/Mix_Me_a_Person" title="Mix Me a Person">Mix Me a Person</a></i> (1962), and composed, arranged and conducted the score for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Amorous_Prawn" title="The Amorous Prawn">The Amorous Prawn</a></i> (also 1962). In 1962, Barry transferred to <a href="/wiki/Ember_Records_(UK_label)" title="Ember Records (UK label)">Ember Records</a>, where he produced albums as well as arranging them.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>These achievements caught the attention of the <a href="/wiki/Film_producer" title="Film producer">producers</a> of a new film called <i><a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(film)" title="Dr. No (film)">Dr. No</a></i> (1962) who were dissatisfied with a theme for <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> given to them by <a href="/wiki/Monty_Norman" title="Monty Norman">Monty Norman</a>. Barry was hired and the result was one of the most famous signature tunes in film history, the "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme" title="James Bond Theme">James Bond Theme</a>". (Credit goes to Monty Norman, <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme#Authorship_of_the_&quot;James_Bond_Theme&quot;" title="James Bond Theme">see here</a>.) When the producers of the Bond series engaged <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Bart" title="Lionel Bart">Lionel Bart</a> to score the next James Bond film <i><a href="/wiki/From_Russia_with_Love_(film)" title="From Russia with Love (film)">From Russia with Love</a></i> (1963), they discovered that Bart could neither read nor write music. Though Bart wrote a title song for the film, the producers remembered Barry\'s arrangement of the James Bond Theme and his composing and arranging for several films with Adam Faith. Lionel Bart also recommended Barry to producer <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baker" title="Stanley Baker">Stanley Baker</a> for his film <i><a href="/wiki/Zulu_(1964_film)" title="Zulu (1964 film)">Zulu</a></i> (1964).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Bart and Barry worked together in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Man_in_the_Middle_(film)" title="Man in the Middle (film)">Man in the Middle</a></i>.\n</p><p>This was the turning point for Barry, and he subsequently won five <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a> and four <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, with scores for, among others,  <i><a href="/wiki/Born_Free" title="Born Free">Born Free</a></i> (1966), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_in_Winter_(1968_film)" title="The Lion in Winter (1968 film)">The Lion in Winter</a></i> (1968), <i><a href="/wiki/Midnight_Cowboy" title="Midnight Cowboy">Midnight Cowboy</a></i> (1969) for which he did not receive an on-screen credit.<sup id="cite_ref-IMDb_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMDb-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Somewhere_in_Time_(film)" title="Somewhere in Time (film)">Somewhere in Time</a></i> (1980).<sup id="cite_ref-one-india_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-one-india-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barry was often cited as having had a distinct style which concentrated on lush strings and extensive use of brass. However he was also an innovator, being one of the first to employ synthesizers in a film score (<i><a href="/wiki/On_Her_Majesty%27s_Secret_Service_(film)" title="On Her Majesty&#39;s Secret Service (film)">On Her Majesty\'s Secret Service</a></i>, also 1969),<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> and to make wide use of pop artists and songs in <i>Midnight Cowboy</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Because Barry provided not just the main title theme but the complete soundtrack <a href="/wiki/Sheet_music" title="Sheet music">score</a>, his music often enhanced the critical reception of a film, notably in <i>Midnight Cowboy</i>, the first remake  of <i><a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(1976_film)" title="King Kong (1976 film)">King Kong</a></i> (1976), <i><a href="/wiki/Out_of_Africa_(film)" title="Out of Africa (film)">Out of Africa</a></i> (1985), and <i><a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Wolves" title="Dances with Wolves">Dances with Wolves</a></i> (1990). Barry would often watch films and would note down with pen and paper what worked or what did not.<sup id="cite_ref-Yorshire_Post_Obit_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yorshire_Post_Obit-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barry composed the theme for the TV series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Persuaders!" title="The Persuaders!">The Persuaders!</a></i> (1971), also known as <i>The Unlucky Heroes</i>, in which <a href="/wiki/Tony_Curtis" title="Tony Curtis">Tony Curtis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roger_Moore" title="Roger Moore">Roger Moore</a> were paired as rich playboys solving crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The instrumental recording features the <a href="/wiki/Cimbalom" title="Cimbalom">Cimbalom</a> (which Barry also used for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ipcress_File_(film)" title="The Ipcress File (film)">The Ipcress File</a></i> (1965) and other themes) and <a href="/wiki/Moog_synthesizer" title="Moog synthesizer">Moog synthesizers</a>. The theme was a hit single in many European countries (including France, Germany, and the Benelux states), contributing to the cult status of the series in Europe, and the record featured Barry\'s <i>The Girl with the Sun in Her Hair</i> on the B side, an instrumental piece featured in a long running TV advert for <a href="/wiki/Sunsilk" title="Sunsilk">Sunsilk</a> shampoo. Barry also wrote the scores to a number of musicals, including the 1965 <i><a href="/wiki/Passion_Flower_Hotel" class="mw-redirect" title="Passion Flower Hotel">Passion Flower Hotel</a></i> (lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Peacock" title="Trevor Peacock">Trevor Peacock</a>), the successful 1974 West End show <i><a href="/wiki/Billy_(musical)" title="Billy (musical)">Billy</a></i> (lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and two major <a href="/wiki/Broadway_musical" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadway musical">Broadway</a> flops, <i><a href="/wiki/Lolita,_My_Love" title="Lolita, My Love">Lolita, My Love</a></i> (1971), with <a href="/wiki/Alan_Jay_Lerner" title="Alan Jay Lerner">Alan Jay Lerner</a> as lyricist, and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Little_Prince_and_the_Aviator" title="The Little Prince and the Aviator">The Little Prince and the Aviator</a></i> (1981), again with lyricist Don Black.\n</p><p>In 2001, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a> conferred an honorary degree on Barry, and in 2002 he was named an Honorary <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_City" title="Freedom of the City">Freeman</a> of the City of York.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During 2006, Barry was the executive producer on an album entitled <i>Here\'s to the Heroes</i> by the Australian ensemble <a href="/wiki/The_Ten_Tenors" title="The Ten Tenors">The Ten Tenors</a>. The album features a number of songs Barry wrote in collaboration with his lyricist friend, Don Black. Barry and Black also composed one of the songs on <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Bassey" title="Shirley Bassey">Shirley Bassey</a>\'s 2009 album, <i>The Performance</i>. The song, entitled "Our Time Is Now", is the first written by the duo for Bassey since "<a href="/wiki/Diamonds_Are_Forever_(soundtrack)" title="Diamonds Are Forever (soundtrack)">Diamonds Are Forever</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="James_Bond_series"><i>James Bond</i> series</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: James Bond series">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After the success of <i>Dr. No</i>, Barry was hired to compose and perform eleven of the next fourteen <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond</a></i> films (<a href="/wiki/Monty_Norman" title="Monty Norman">Monty Norman</a> is legally recognised as the composer of the "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme" title="James Bond Theme">James Bond Theme</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph-obit_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-obit-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In his tenure with the film series, Barry\'s music, variously brassy and moody, achieved very wide appeal. For <i>From Russia with Love</i> he composed "007", an alternative James Bond signature theme, which is featured in four other Bond films (<i>Thunderball</i>, <i>You Only Live Twice</i>, <i>Diamonds Are Forever</i> and <i>Moonraker</i>). The theme "Stalking", for the teaser sequence of <i>From Russia with Love</i>, was covered by colleague <a href="/wiki/Marvin_Hamlisch" title="Marvin Hamlisch">Marvin Hamlisch</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Spy_Who_Loved_Me_(film)" title="The Spy Who Loved Me (film)">The Spy Who Loved Me</a></i> (1977). (The music and lyrics for <i>From Russia with Love\'</i>s title song were written by <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Bart" title="Lionel Bart">Lionel Bart</a>, whose musical theatre credits included <i>Oliver!</i>) Barry also contributed indirectly to the soundtrack of the spoof version of <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(1967_film)" title="Casino Royale (1967 film)">Casino Royale</a></i> (1967): his <i><a href="/wiki/Born_Free" title="Born Free">Born Free</a></i> theme appears briefly in the opening sequence.\n</p><p>In <i><a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(film)" title="Goldfinger (film)">Goldfinger</a></i> (1964), he perfected the "Bond sound", a heady mixture of brass, jazz elements and sensuous melodies. There is even an element of Barry\'s jazz roots in the big-band track "Into Miami", which follows the title credits and accompanies the film\'s iconic image of the camera lens zooming toward the Fontainebleau Hotel in <a href="/wiki/Miami_Beach" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami Beach">Miami Beach</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a> was working as a session guitarist at the time, and was a part of the recording sessions for the "Goldfinger" soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> For Bond films, session musicians such as Page were relegated to the instrumental/score versions of songs, while the main musicians (on Goldfinger such as <a href="/wiki/Vic_Flick" title="Vic Flick">Vic Flick</a>) were given the main film theme song to record .<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Thus, Flick is heard as lead guitarist on the main theme, leaving Page as a background acoustic contributor to Flick on the instrumental version of the song.\n</p><p>Barry\'s love for the Russian romantic composers is often reflected in his music; in his Bond scores he unites this with brass-heavy jazz writing. His use of strings, lyricism, half-diminished chords, and complex key shifting provides melancholy contrast - in his scores this is often heard in variations of the title songs that are used to underscore plot development.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As Barry matured, the Bond scores became more lushly melodic (along with other scores of his such as <i><a href="/wiki/Out_of_Africa_(film)" title="Out of Africa (film)">Out of Africa</a></i>), as in <i><a href="/wiki/Moonraker_(film)" title="Moonraker (film)">Moonraker</a></i> (1979) and <i><a href="/wiki/Octopussy" title="Octopussy">Octopussy</a></i> (1983). Barry\'s score for <i>A View to a Kill</i> was traditional, but his collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">Duran Duran</a> for the <a href="/wiki/A_View_to_a_Kill_(song)" title="A View to a Kill (song)">title song</a> was contemporary and reached number one in the United States and number two in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>. Both <i>A View to a Kill</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Living_Daylights_(soundtrack)" title="The Living Daylights (soundtrack)">The Living Daylights</a></i> theme by <a href="/wiki/A-ha" title="A-ha">a-ha</a> blended the pop music style of the bands with Barry\'s orchestration. In 2006, a-ha\'s <a href="/wiki/Pal_Waaktaar" class="mw-redirect" title="Pal Waaktaar">Pal Waaktaar</a> complimented Barry\'s contributions: "I loved the stuff he added to the track, I mean it gave it this really cool string arrangement. That\'s when for me it started to sound like a Bond thing."<sup id="cite_ref-UKC4TV_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UKC4TV-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barry\'s last score for the Bond series was <i><a href="/wiki/The_Living_Daylights" title="The Living Daylights">The Living Daylights</a></i> (1987), <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Dalton" title="Timothy Dalton">Timothy Dalton</a>\'s first film in the series with Barry making a cameo appearance as a conductor in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Barry was intended to score <i><a href="/wiki/Licence_to_Kill" title="Licence to Kill">Licence to Kill</a></i> (1989) but was recovering from throat surgery at the time and it was considered unsafe to fly him to London to complete the score. The score was completed by <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kamen" title="Michael Kamen">Michael Kamen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/David_Arnold" title="David Arnold">David Arnold</a>, a British composer, saw the result of two years\' work in 1997 with the release of <i>Shaken and Stirred: The David Arnold James Bond Project</i>, an album of new versions of the themes from various James Bond films. Arnold thanks Barry in the sleeve notes, referring to him as "the Guvnor". Almost all of the tracks were John Barry compositions, and the revision of his work met with his approval&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 he contacted <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Broccoli" title="Barbara Broccoli">Barbara Broccoli</a>, producer of the then upcoming <i><a href="/wiki/Tomorrow_Never_Dies" title="Tomorrow Never Dies">Tomorrow Never Dies</a></i>, to recommend Arnold as the film\'s composer.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Arnold also went on to score four subsequent Bond films: <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Is_Not_Enough" title="The World Is Not Enough">The World Is Not Enough</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Another_Day" title="Die Another Day">Die Another Day</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_Royale_(2006_film)" title="Casino Royale (2006 film)">Casino Royale</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Quantum_of_Solace" title="Quantum of Solace">Quantum of Solace</a></i>.\n</p><p>Sole compositional credit for the "James Bond Theme" is assigned to <a href="/wiki/Monty_Norman" title="Monty Norman">Monty Norman</a>, who was contracted as composer for <i>Dr. No</i>. Some 30 years later, in 2001, the disputed authorship of the theme was examined legally in the High Court in London after Norman sued <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sunday Times (UK)">The Sunday Times</a></i> for publishing an article in 1997 in which Barry was named as the true composer; Barry testified for the defence.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tweedie_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tweedie-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In court, Barry testified that he had been handed a musical manuscript of a work by Norman (meant to become the theme) and that he was to arrange it musically, and that he composed additional music and arranged the "James Bond Theme". The court was also told that Norman received sole credit because of his prior contract with the producers. Barry said that a deal was struck whereby he would receive a flat fee of \xc2\xa3250 and Norman would receive the songwriting credit.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Libel_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Libel-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Barry said that he had accepted the deal with United Artists Head of Music Noel Rogers because it would help his career. Despite these claims the jury ruled unanimously in favour of Norman.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Libel_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Libel-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 7 September 2006, John Barry publicly defended his authorship of the theme on the <a href="/wiki/Steve_Wright_(DJ)" title="Steve Wright (DJ)">Steve Wright</a> show on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">BBC Radio 2</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life_and_death">Personal life and death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Personal life and death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Barry was married four times. His first three marriages, to Barbara Pickard (1959\xe2\x80\x9363), <a href="/wiki/Jane_Birkin" title="Jane Birkin">Jane Birkin</a> (1965\xe2\x80\x9368), and Jane Sidey (1969\xe2\x80\x9378) all ended in divorce.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_Obit_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_Obit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He was married to his fourth wife, Laurie, from January 1978<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_Obit_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_Obit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> until his death. The couple had a son, Jonpatrick. Barry had three daughters, Suzanne (Susie) with his first wife, Barbara, <a href="/wiki/Kate_Barry_(photographer)" title="Kate Barry (photographer)">Kate</a> with his second wife, Jane, and Sian from a relationship with Ulla Larson between the first two marriages.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Obit_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Obit-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Suzy Barry, who is married to BBC business journalist <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jack" title="Simon Jack">Simon Jack</a>, is the mother of his two granddaughters, Phoebe and Florence Ingleby.\n</p><p>In 1975 Barry moved to California. A British judge later accused him of emigrating to avoid paying <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>134,000 due the <a href="/wiki/Inland_Revenue" title="Inland Revenue">Inland Revenue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_Obit_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_Obit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The matter was resolved in the late 1980s and Barry was able to return to the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Telegraph_Obit_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraph_Obit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He subsequently lived for many years in the United States, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Oyster_Bay_(hamlet),_New_York" title="Oyster Bay (hamlet), New York">Oyster Bay</a>, New York, in <a href="/wiki/Centre_Island,_New_York" title="Centre Island, New York">Centre Island</a> on <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a>, from 1980.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian_Obit_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian_Obit-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barry suffered a <a href="/wiki/Boerhaave_syndrome" title="Boerhaave syndrome">rupture of the oesophagus</a> in 1988, following a toxic reaction to a health tonic he had consumed. The incident rendered him unable to work for two years and left him vulnerable to <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Barry died of a heart attack on 30 January 2011 at his Oyster Bay home, aged 77.<sup id="cite_ref-variety.com_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety.com-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A memorial concert took place on 20 June 2011 at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> in London where the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Royal Philharmonic Orchestra">Royal Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shirley_Bassey" title="Shirley Bassey">Shirley Bassey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rumer_(musician)" title="Rumer (musician)">Rumer</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Arnold" title="David Arnold">David Arnold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wynne_Evans" title="Wynne Evans">Wynne Evans</a> and others performed Barry\'s music.<sup id="cite_ref-entertainmentartsbbc_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entertainmentartsbbc-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Martin" title="George Martin">Sir George Martin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Parkinson" title="Michael Parkinson">Sir Michael Parkinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Dalton" title="Timothy Dalton">Timothy Dalton</a> and others also contributed to the celebration of his life and work.<sup id="cite_ref-variety.com_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-variety.com-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-entertainmentartsbbc_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entertainmentartsbbc-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Barry_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Barry-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The event was sponsored by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Music" title="Royal College of Music">Royal College of Music</a> through a grant by the <a href="/wiki/Albert_R._Broccoli" title="Albert R. Broccoli">Broccoli</a> Foundation.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 1999 Barry was made an <a href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">Officer of the Order of the British Empire</a> (OBE) at <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a> for services to music, and received the <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Academy_Fellowship_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="BAFTA Academy Fellowship Award">BAFTA Academy Fellowship Award</a> in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Barry_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Barry-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> ranked Barry\'s score for <i>Out of Africa</i> No. 15 on <a href="/wiki/AFI%27s_100_Years_of_Film_Scores" title="AFI&#39;s 100 Years of Film Scores">their list of the greatest film scores</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> His scores for the following films were also nominated:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Goldfinger</i> (1964)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Born_Free" title="Born Free">Born Free</a></i> (1966)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_in_Winter_(1968_film)" title="The Lion in Winter (1968 film)">The Lion in Winter</a></i> (1968)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Somewhere_in_Time_(film)" title="Somewhere in Time (film)">Somewhere in Time</a></i> (1980)</li>\n<li><i>Body Heat</i> (1981)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Wolves" title="Dances with Wolves">Dances with Wolves</a></i> (1990)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a soundtracks for the following James Bond films (title song collaborators in brackets):\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Dr._No_(soundtrack)" title="Dr. No (soundtrack)">Dr. No</a></i> (1962)&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme" title="James Bond Theme">James Bond Theme</a></i> (composed by <a href="/wiki/Monty_Norman" title="Monty Norman">Monty Norman</a>) as arranged by Barry used on main and end titles, and key points such as Bond\'s arrival in Jamaica</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/From_Russia_with_Love_(soundtrack)" title="From Russia with Love (soundtrack)">From Russia with Love</a></i> (lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Bart" title="Lionel Bart">Lionel Bart</a>) (1963)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Goldfinger_(soundtrack)" title="Goldfinger (soundtrack)">Goldfinger</a></i> (lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Newley" title="Anthony Newley">Anthony Newley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Bricusse" title="Leslie Bricusse">Leslie Bricusse</a>), (1964)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Thunderball_(soundtrack)" title="Thunderball (soundtrack)">Thunderball</a></i> (lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Don_Black_(lyricist)" title="Don Black (lyricist)">Don Black</a>) (1965)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(soundtrack)" title="You Only Live Twice (soundtrack)">You Only Live Twice</a></i> (lyrics by Leslie Bricusse) (1967)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/Octopussy_(soundtrack)" title="Octopussy (soundtrack)">Octopussy</a></i> (lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Tim_Rice" title="Tim Rice">Tim Rice</a>) (1983)</li>\n<li><i><a (1985)</li>\n<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Living_Daylights_(soundtrack)" title="The Living Daylights (soundtrack)">The Living Daylights</a></i> (music and lyrics by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Waaktaar-Savoy" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>(Excludes co-composed hits, e.g. <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">Duran Duran</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/A_View_to_a_Kill_(song)" title="A View to a Kill (song)">A View to a Kill</a></i>)\n</p>\n<ul><li>"Hit and Miss" as The John Barry Seven plus Four, UK#10 (first charted 1960)</li>\n<li>"Beat for Beatniks" as The John Barry Orchestra, UK#40 (1960)</li>\n<li>"Never Let Go" as The John Barry Orchestra, UK#49 (1960)</li>\n<li>"Blueberry Hill" as The John Barry Orchestra, UK#34 (1960)</li>\n<li>"Walk Don\'t Run" as The John Barry Seven, UK#11 (1960)</li>\n<li>"Black Stockings" as The John Barry Seven, UK#27 (1960)</li>\n<li>"<a href="/wiki/The_Magnificent_Seven" title="The Magnificent Seven">The Magnificent Seven</a>" as The John Barry Seven, UK#45 (1961)</li>\n<li>"Cutty Sark" as The John Barry Seven, UK#35 (1962)</li>\n<li>"The <a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme" title="James Bond Theme">James Bond Theme</a>" as The John Barry Orchestra, UK#13 (1962)</li>\n<li>"From Russia with Love" as The John Barry Orchestra, UK#39 (1963)</li>\n<li>"Theme from \'The Persuaders\'" as John Barry, UK#13 (1971)</li></ul>\n<p>His four highest-charting hits all spent more than 10 weeks in the UK top 50.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sampled_by_other_artists">Sampled by other artists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sampled by other artists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Barry\'s work began to be sampled in the 1990s by artists such as <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a>, with his "<a href="/wiki/James_Bond_Theme" title="James Bond Theme">James Bond Theme</a>" being sampled by performers as diverse as <a href="/wiki/Bonobo" title="Bonobo">Bonobo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gang_Starr" title="Gang Starr">Gang Starr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Junior_Reid" title="Junior Reid">Junior Reid</a>. <a href="/wiki/Fatboy_Slim" title="Fatboy Slim">Fatboy Slim</a> used the opening guitars from "Beat Girl (Main Title)" for "<a href="/wiki/Rockafeller_Skank" class="mw-redirect" title="Rockafeller Skank">Rockafeller Skank</a>" from his album, <i><a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Come_a_Long_Way,_Baby" title="You&#39;ve Come a Long Way, Baby">You\'ve Come a Long Way, Baby</a></i> (1998). <a href="/wiki/The_Sneaker_Pimps" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sneaker Pimps">The Sneaker Pimps</a> also sampled "Golden Girl" on their single "<a href="/wiki/6_Underground" title="6 Underground">6 Underground</a>" (1996). Additionally, "You Only Live Twice" was heavily sampled on "<a href="/wiki/Millennium_(song)" title="Millennium (song)">Millennium</a>" from <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Williams" title="Robbie Williams">Robbie Williams</a>\' second album, <i><a href="/wiki/I%27ve_Been_Expecting_You" title="I&#39;ve Been Expecting You">I\'ve Been Expecting You</a></i>. Barry was set to compose <i><a href="/wiki/Thomas_and_the_Magic_Railroad" title="Thomas and the Magic Railroad">Thomas and the Magic Railroad</a></i> but left due to scheduling conflicts.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Barry_(composer)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>The Sunday Times Magazine</i> (London). 18 December 2011. p. 64.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-one-india-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-one-india_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-one-india_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.is/20130218050401/http://entertainment.oneindia.in/hollywood/top-stories/scoop/2011/james-bond-composer-john-barry-dies-010211.html">"<span class="cs1-kern-left">\'</span>James Bond Theme\' composer John Barry dies of heart attack"</a>.
